       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      That year
      <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">
       John Cabot
      </a>
      , also a commissioned Italian, got
      <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">
       letters patent
      </a>
      from King
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">
       Henry VII of England
      </a>
      . Sailing from
      <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">
       Bristol
      </a>
      , probably backed by the local
      <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Merchant_Venturers" title="Society of Merchant Venturers">
       Society of Merchant Venturers
      </a>
      , Cabot crossed the Atlantic from a northerly latitude hoping the voyage to the "West Indies" would be shorter
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and made a landfall somewhere in North America, possibly
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="History of Newfoundland and Labrador">
       Newfoundland
      </a>
      . In 1499
      <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Fernandes_Lavrador" title="Joo Fernandes Lavrador">
       Joo Fernandes Lavrador
      </a>
      was licensed by the King of Portugal and together with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_de_Barcelos" title="Pro de Barcelos">
       Pro de Barcelos
      </a>
      they first sighted
      <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">
       Labrador
      </a>
      , which was granted and named after him. After returning he possibly went to Bristol to sail in the name of England.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nearly at the same time, between 1499 and 1502 brothers
      <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">
       Gaspar
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Corte-Real" title="Miguel Corte-Real">
       Miguel Corte Real
      </a>
      explored and named the coasts of
      <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">
       Greenland
      </a>
      and also Newfoundland.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Both explorations signaled in 1502
      <a href="/wiki/Cantino_planisphere" title="Cantino planisphere">
       Cantino planisphere
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22True_Indies.22_and_Brazil">
       The "True Indies" and Brazil
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title='Edit section: The "True Indies" and Brazil'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In 1497, newly crowned King
      <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">
       Manuel I of Portugal
      </a>
      sent an exploratory fleet eastwards, fulfilling his predecessor's project of finding a route to the Indies. In July 1499 news spread that the Portuguese had reached the "true indies", as a letter was dispatched by the Portuguese king to the Spanish Catholic Monarchs one day after the celebrated return of the fleet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The third expedition by Columbus in 1498 was the beginning of the first successful Spanish colonization in the
      <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">
       West Indies
      </a>
      , on the island of Hispaniola. Despite growing doubts, Columbus refused to accept that he had not reached the Indies. During the voyage he discovered the mouth of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" title="Orinoco River">
       Orinoco River
      </a>
      on the north coast of South America (now Venezuela) and thought that the huge quantity of fresh water coming from it could only be from a continental land mass, which he was certain was the Asian mainland.
     </p>
     <p>
      As shipping between
      <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
       Seville
      </a>
      and the West Indies grew, knowledge of the Caribbean islands, Central America and the northern coast of South America grew. One of these Spanish fleets, that of
      <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">
       Alonso de Ojeda
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">
       Amerigo Vespucci
      </a>
      in 1499-1500, reached land at the coast of what is now
      <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">
       Guyana
      </a>
      , when the two explorers seem to have separated in opposite directions. Vespucci sailed southward, discovering the mouth of the
      <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">
       Amazon River
      </a>
      in July 1499,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pohl1966_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pohl1966-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and reaching 6S, in present-day north east
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      , before turning around.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the beginning of 1500
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vicente_Y%C3%A1%C3%B1ez_Pinzon" title="Vicente Yez Pinzon">
       Vicente Yez Pinzon
      </a>
      was blown off course by a storm and reached what is now the north east coast of Brazil in 26 January 1500, exploring as far south as the present-day state of
      <a href="/wiki/Pernambuco" title="Pernambuco">
       Pernambuco
      </a>
      . His fleet was the first to fully enter the Amazon River estuary which he named
      <i>
       Ro Santa Mara de la Mar Dulce
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       Saint Mary's River of the Sweet Sea
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morison1974_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Morison1974-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the land was too far east for the Spanish to claim under the Treaty of Tordesillas, but the discovery created Spanish interest, with a second voyage by Pinzon in 1508 and a voyage in 151516 by a navigator of the 1508 expedition,
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_D%C3%ADaz_de_Sol%C3%ADs" title="Juan Daz de Sols">
       Juan Daz de Sols
      </a>
      . The 151516 expedition was spurred on by reports of Portuguese exploration of the region (see below). It ended when de Sols and some of his crew disappeared when exploring a
      <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Ro de la Plata">
       River Plate
      </a>
      river in a boat, but what it found re-ignited Spanish interest, and colonization began in 1531.
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 1500, the
      <a href="/wiki/2nd_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Cabral,_1500)" title="2nd Portuguese India Armada (Cabral, 1500)">
       second Portuguese India Armada
      </a>
      , headed by
      <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro lvares Cabral">
       Pedro lvares Cabral
      </a>
      , with a crew of expert captains, including Bartolomeu Dias and
      <a href="/wiki/Nicolau_Coelho" title="Nicolau Coelho">
       Nicolau Coelho
      </a>
      , encountered the Brazilian coast as it swung westward in the Atlantic while performing a large "
      <a href="/wiki/Volta_do_mar" title="Volta do mar">
       volta do mar
      </a>
      " to avoid becalming in the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">
       Gulf of Guinea
      </a>
      . On 21 April 1500 a mountain was seen and was named
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monte_Pascoal" title="Monte Pascoal">
        Monte Pascoal
       </a>
      </i>
      , and on the 22 April Cabral landed on the coast. On the 25 April the entire fleet sailed into the harbor they named
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Porto_Seguro" title="Porto Seguro">
        Porto Seguro
       </a>
      </i>
      (Port Secure). Cabral perceived that the new land lay east of the line of Tordesillas, and sent an envoy to Portugal with the discovery in letters, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Carta_de_P%C3%AAro_Vaz_de_Caminha" title="Carta de Pro Vaz de Caminha">
       letter
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pero_Vaz_de_Caminha" title="Pero Vaz de Caminha">
       Pero Vaz de Caminha
      </a>
      . Believing the land to be an island, he named it
      <a href="/wiki/Ilha_de_Vera_Cruz" title="Ilha de Vera Cruz">
       Ilha de Vera Cruz
      </a>
      (Island of the True Cross).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some historians have suggested that the Portuguese may have encountered the South American bulge earlier while sailing the "volta do mar", hence the insistence of John II in moving the line west of Tordesillasso his landing in Brazil may not have been an accident; although John's motivation may have simply been to increase the chance of claiming new lands in the Atlantic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      From the east coast, the fleet then turned eastward to resume the journey to the southern tip of Africa and India. Cabral was the first captain to touch four continents, leading the first expedition that connected and united Europe, Africa, the New World, and Asia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the invitation of king Manuel I of Portugal, Amerigo Vespucci
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
       a Florentine who had been working for a branch of the
      <a href="/wiki/Medici_Bank" title="Medici Bank">
       Medici Bank
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
       Seville
      </a>
      since 1491, fitting oceanic expeditions and travelling twice to
      <a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">
       The Guianas
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cosa" title="Juan de la Cosa">
       Juan de la Cosa
      </a>
      in the service of Spain
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
       participated as observer in these exploratory voyages to the east coast of South America. The expeditions became widely known in Europe after two accounts attributed to him, published between 1502 and 1504, suggested that the newly discovered lands were not the Indies but a "
      <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
       New World
      </a>
      ",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <i>
       Mundus novus
      </i>
      , Latin title of a contemporary document based on Vespucci letters to
      <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_di_Pierfrancesco_de%27_Medici" title="Lorenzo di Pierfrancesco de' Medici">
       Lorenzo di Pierfrancesco de' Medici
      </a>
      , which had become widely popular in Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was soon understood that Columbus had not reached Asia but had found a new continent, the Americas.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/America_(name)" title="America (name)">
       The Americas were named
      </a>
      in 1507 by
      <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">
       cartographers
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Waldseem%C3%BCller_map" title="Waldseemller map">
       Martin Waldseemller
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann" title="Matthias Ringmann">
       Matthias Ringmann
      </a>
      , probably after Amerigo Vespucci.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 15011502, one of these Portuguese expeditions, led by
      <a href="/wiki/Gon%C3%A7alo_Coelho" title="Gonalo Coelho">
       Gonalo Coelho
      </a>
      , sailed south along the coast of South America to the bay of present day
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
       Rio de Janeiro
      </a>
      . Amerigo Vespucci`s account states that the expedition reached the latitude "South Pole elevation 52 S", in the "cold" latitudes of what is now southern
      <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">
       Patagonia
      </a>
      (possibly near the Strait), before turning back. Vespucci wrote that they headed toward the southwest and south, following "a long, unbending coastline" (apparently coincident with the southern South American coast). This seems controversial, since he changed part of his description in the subsequent letter, stating a shift, from about 32 S (Southern Brazil), to south-southeast, to open sea; maintaining, however, that they reached 50/52 S (if it was by his own decision or by D. Manuel`s censors who had to pressure him to alter his account, because he had revealed far too much to Lorenzo de' Medici and into the public domain, is unknown).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1503,
      <a href="/wiki/Binot_Paulmier_de_Gonneville" title="Binot Paulmier de Gonneville">
       Binot Paulmier de Gonneville
      </a>
      , challenging the Portuguese policy of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mare_clausum" title="Mare clausum">
        mare clausum
       </a>
      </i>
      , led one of the earliest
      <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
       French
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">
       Normand
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">
       Breton
      </a>
      expeditions to Brazil. He intended to sail to the East Indies, but near the Cape of Good Hope his ship was diverted to west by a storm, and landed in the present day state of
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">
       Santa Catarina
      </a>
      (southern Brazil), in 5 January 1504.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guti%C3%A9rrez,_the_Americas,_1562.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5148" data-file-width="5246" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Guti%C3%A9rrez%2C_the_Americas%2C_1562.jpg/220px-Guti%C3%A9rrez%2C_the_Americas%2C_1562.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Guti%C3%A9rrez%2C_the_Americas%2C_1562.jpg/330px-Guti%C3%A9rrez%2C_the_Americas%2C_1562.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Guti%C3%A9rrez%2C_the_Americas%2C_1562.jpg/440px-Guti%C3%A9rrez%2C_the_Americas%2C_1562.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guti%C3%A9rrez,_the_Americas,_1562.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Americae_Sive_Quartae_Orbis_Partis_Nova_Et_Exactissima_Descriptio" title="Americae Sive Quartae Orbis Partis Nova Et Exactissima Descriptio">
          Americae Sive Quartae Orbis Partis Nova Et Exactissima Descriptio
         </a>
        </i>
        , the largest map of the Americas until the 17th century and the first map to use the name "California".
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1511-1512, Portuguese captains
      <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_de_Lisboa" title="Joo de Lisboa">
       Joo de Lisboa
      </a>
      and Estevo de Fris reached the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_de_La_Plata" title="Rio de La Plata">
       River Plate
      </a>
      estuary in the present-day
      <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
       Uruguay
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
       Argentina
      </a>
      , and went as far south as the present-day
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_San_Matias" title="Gulf of San Matias">
       Gulf of San Matias
      </a>
      at 42S (recorded in the
      <i>
       Newen Zeytung auss Pressilandt
      </i>
      meaning "New Tidings from the Land of Brazil").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The expedition reachead a cape extending north to south which they called Cape of "Santa Maria" (
      <a href="/wiki/Punta_del_Este" title="Punta del Este">
       Punta del Este
      </a>
      , keeping the name the Cape nearby); and after 40S they found a "Cape" or "a point or place extending into the sea", and a "Gulf" (in June and July). After they had navigated for nearly 300km (186mi) to round the cape, they again sighted the continent on the other side, and steered towards the northwest, but a storm prevented them from making any headway. Driven away by the
      <i>
       Tramontane
      </i>
      or north wind, they retraced their course. Also gives the first news of the
      <i>
       White King
      </i>
      and the "people of the mountains" to the interior (the
      <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
       Inca Empire
      </a>
      ), and a gift, an ax of silver, obtained from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charr%C3%BAa" title="Charra">
       Charra
      </a>
      natives on their return ("to the coast or side of
      <i>
       Brazil
      </i>
      "), and "to West" (along the coast and the River Plate estuary), and offered to King Manuel I.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_de_Haro" title="Christopher de Haro">
       Christopher de Haro
      </a>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">
       Flemish
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic" title="Sephardic">
       Sephardic
      </a>
      origin (one of the financiers of the expedition along with D. Nuno Manuel), who would serve the Spanish Crown after 1516, believed that the navigators had discovered a southern
      <i>
       strait
      </i>
      to west and Asia.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1519, an expedition sent by the Spanish Crown to find a way to Asia was led by the experienced Portuguese navigator
      <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
       Ferdinand Magellan
      </a>
      . The fleet explored the rivers and bays as it charted the South American coast until it found a way to the Pacific Ocean through the
      <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">
       Strait of Magellan
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 15241525,
      <a href="/wiki/Aleixo_Garcia" title="Aleixo Garcia">
       Aleixo Garcia
      </a>
      , a Portuguese conquistador (possible a veteran of the Sols expedition of 1516), led a private expedition of a few shipwrecked Spanish and Portuguese adventurers, that recruited about 2000
      <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaran people">
       Guaran Indians
      </a>
      . They explored the territories of present-day southern Brazil,
      <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
       Paraguay
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
       Bolivia
      </a>
      , using the native trail network, the
      <i>
       Peabiru
      </i>
      . They were also the first Europeans to cross the
      <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">
       Chaco
      </a>
      and reach the outer territories of the Inca Empire on the hills of the
      <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
       Andes
      </a>
      , near
      <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">
       Sucre
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_Ocean_.281497.E2.80.931513.29">
       Indian Ocean (14971513)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Indian Ocean (14971513)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Gama.27s_route_to_India">
       Gama's route to India
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gama's route to India">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" title="Portuguese India Armadas">
       Portuguese India Armadas
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="556" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png/200px-Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png/300px-Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png/400px-Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caminho_maritimo_para_a_India.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">
         Vasco da Gama
        </a>
        's 14971499 travel to India (black). Previous travels of
        <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_da_Covilh%C3%A3" title="Pro da Covilh">
         Pro da Covilh
        </a>
        (orange) and
        <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Paiva" title="Afonso de Paiva">
         Afonso de Paiva
        </a>
        (blue), and their common route (green)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Protected from direct Spanish competition by the treaty of Tordesillas, Portuguese eastward exploration and colonization continued apace. Twice, in 1485 and 1488, Portugal officially rejected
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
       Christopher Columbus
      </a>
      's idea of reaching India by sailing westwards. King
      <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">
       John II of Portugal
      </a>
      's experts rejected it, for they held the opinion that Columbus's estimation of a travel distance of 2,400 miles (3,860km) was undervalued,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in part because
      <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">
       Bartolomeu Dias
      </a>
      departed in 1487 trying the rounding of the southern tip of Africa, therefore they believed that sailing east would require a far shorter journey. Dias's return from the
      <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">
       Cape of Good Hope
      </a>
      in 1488, and
      <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_da_Covilh%C3%A3" title="Pro da Covilh">
       Pro da Covilh
      </a>
      travel to
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopia
      </a>
      overland indicated that the richness of the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">
       Indian Sea
      </a>
      was accessible from the Atlantic. A long-overdue expedition was prepared.
     </p>
     <p>
      Under new king
      <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">
       Manuel I of Portugal
      </a>
      , on July 1497 a small exploratory fleet of four ships and about 170 men left
      <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">
       Lisbon
      </a>
      under command of
      <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">
       Vasco da Gama
      </a>
      . By December the fleet passed the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Fish_River" title="Great Fish River">
       Great Fish River
      </a>
      where Dias had turned backand sailed into unknown waters. On 20 May 1498, they arrived at
      <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">
       Calicut
      </a>
      . The efforts of Vasco da Gama to get favorable trading conditions were hampered by the low value of their goods, compared with the valuable goods traded there. Two years and two days after departure, Gama and a survivor crew of 55 men returned in glory to Portugal as the first ships to sail directly from Europe to India.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1500, a second, larger fleet of thirteen ships and about 1500 men was sent to India. Under command of
      <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro lvares Cabral">
       Pedro lvares Cabral
      </a>
      they made a first landfall on the Brazilian coast; later, in the Indian Ocean, one of Cabral's ships reached
      <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">
       Madagascar
      </a>
      (1501), which was partly explored by
      <a href="/wiki/Trist%C3%A3o_da_Cunha" title="Tristo da Cunha">
       Tristo da Cunha
      </a>
      in 1507;
      <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">
       Mauritius
      </a>
      was discovered in 1507,
      <a href="/wiki/Socotra" title="Socotra">
       Socotra
      </a>
      occupied in 1506. In the same year
      <a href="/wiki/Louren%C3%A7o_de_Almeida" title="Loureno de Almeida">
       Loureno de Almeida
      </a>
      landed in
      <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">
       Sri Lanka
      </a>
      , the eastern island named "
      <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Names of Sri Lanka">
       Taprobane
      </a>
      " in remote accounts of
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
       Alexander the Great
      </a>
      's and 4th-century BCE Greek
      <a href="/wiki/Geographer" title="Geographer">
       geographer
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Megasthenes" title="Megasthenes">
       Megasthenes
      </a>
      . On the Asiatic mainland the first
      <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">
       factories (trading-posts)
      </a>
      were established at Kochi and Calicut (1501) and then
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Goa" title="Old Goa">
       Goa
      </a>
      (1510).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22Spice_Islands.22_and_China">
       The "Spice Islands" and China
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title='Edit section: The "Spice Islands" and China'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malaccaship.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2256" data-file-width="1496" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Malaccaship.JPG/150px-Malaccaship.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Malaccaship.JPG/225px-Malaccaship.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Malaccaship.JPG/300px-Malaccaship.JPG 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malaccaship.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Replica of
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Flor_de_la_Mar" title="Flor de la Mar">
          Flor de la Mar
         </a>
        </i>
        <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">
         carrack
        </a>
        housing the Maritime Museum of
        <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">
         Malacca
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1511,
      <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">
       Afonso de Albuquerque
      </a>
      conquered
      <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">
       Malacca
      </a>
      for Portugal, then the center of Asian trade. East of Malacca, Albuquerque sent several diplomatic missions:
      <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Fernandes" title="Duarte Fernandes">
       Duarte Fernandes
      </a>
      as the first European envoy to the
      <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">
       Kingdom of Siam
      </a>
      (modern
      <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">
       Thailand
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      Getting to know the secret location of the so-called "spice islands"the
      <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">
       Maluku Islands
      </a>
      , mainly the
      <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands" title="Banda Islands">
       Banda
      </a>
      , then the single world source of
      <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">
       nutmeg
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Clove" title="Clove">
       cloves
      </a>
      , main purpose for the travels in the Indian seahe sent an expedition led by
      <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Abreu" title="Antnio de Abreu">
       Antnio de Abreu
      </a>
      to Banda, where they were the first Europeans to arrive in early 1512.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Abreu then left for
      <a href="/wiki/Ambon_Island" title="Ambon Island">
       Ambon Island
      </a>
      while his vice-captain
      <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco Serro">
       Francisco Serro
      </a>
      sank off
      <a href="/wiki/Ternate" title="Ternate">
       Ternate
      </a>
      , where he obtained a license to build a Portuguese fortress-factory: the Fort of So Joo Baptista de Ternate, which founded the Portuguese presence in the
      <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">
       Malay Archipelago
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 1513
      <a href="/wiki/Jorge_%C3%81lvares" title="Jorge lvares">
       Jorge lvares
      </a>
      , one of the Portuguese envoys, reached China. Although he was the first to land on
      <a href="/wiki/Nei_Lingding_Island" title="Nei Lingding Island">
       Lintin Island
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">
       Pearl River Delta
      </a>
      , it was
      <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Perestrello" title="Rafael Perestrello">
       Rafael Perestrello
      </a>
      a cousin of the famed
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
       Christopher Columbus
      </a>
      who became the first European explorer to land on the southern coast of mainland China and trade in
      <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">
       Guangzhou
      </a>
      in 1516, commanding a
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      vessel with a crew from a Malaysian junk that had sailed from
      <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">
       Malacca
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Pires_de_Andrade" title="Ferno Pires de Andrade">
       Ferno Pires de Andrade
      </a>
      visited Canton in 1517 and opened up trade with China. The Portuguese were defeated by the Chinese in 1521 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tunmen" title="Battle of Tunmen">
       Battle of Tunmen
      </a>
      and in 1522 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Xicaowan" title="Battle of Xicaowan">
       Battle of Xicaowan
      </a>
      , during which the Chinese captured Portuguese
      <a href="/wiki/Breech-loading_swivel_gun" title="Breech-loading swivel gun">
       breech-loading swivel guns
      </a>
      and reverse engineered the technology, calling them "Folangji"  (
      <a href="/wiki/Franks#Legacy" title="Franks">
       Frankish
      </a>
      ) guns, since the Portuguese were called "Folangji" by the Chinese. After a few decades, hostilies between the Portuguese and Chinese ceased and in 1557 the Chinese allowed the Portuguese to occupy
      <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">
       Macau
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      To enforce a trade monopoly,
      <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">
       Hormuz
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
       Persian Gulf
      </a>
      was seized by
      <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">
       Afonso de Albuquerque
      </a>
      in 1507 and 1515, who also entered into
      <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">
       diplomatic relations
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
       Persia
      </a>
      . In 1513 while trying to conquer
      <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">
       Aden
      </a>
      , an expedition led by Albuquerque cruised the
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
       Red Sea
      </a>
      inside the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bab_al-Mandab" title="Bab al-Mandab">
       Bab al-Mandab
      </a>
      , and sheltered at
      <a href="/wiki/Kamaran" title="Kamaran">
       Kamaran
      </a>
      island. In 1521, a force under
      <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Correia_(admiral)" title="Antnio Correia (admiral)">
       Antnio Correia
      </a>
      conquered
      <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">
       Bahrain
      </a>
      ushering in a period of almost eighty years of Portuguese rule of the Gulf archipelago.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the Red Sea,
      <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">
       Massawa
      </a>
      was the most northerly point frequented by the Portuguese until 1541, when a fleet under
      <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_da_Gama_(16th_century)" title="Estvo da Gama (16th century)">
       Estevo da Gama
      </a>
      penetrated as far as
      <a href="/wiki/Suez" title="Suez">
       Suez
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_Ocean_.281513.E2.80.931529.29">
       Pacific Ocean (15131529)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Pacific Ocean (15131529)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="316" data-file-width="581" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG/200px-Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG/300px-Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG/400px-Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Balboa_Voyage_1513.PNG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco Nez de Balboa">
         Vasco Nez de Balboa
        </a>
        's travel to the "
        <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
         South Sea
        </a>
        ", 1513
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_of_the_Pacific_Ocean">
       Discovery of the Pacific Ocean
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Discovery of the Pacific Ocean">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1513, about 40 miles (64 kilometres) south of
      <a href="/wiki/Acand%C3%AD" title="Acand">
       Acand
      </a>
      , in present day
      <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
       Colombia
      </a>
      , Spanish
      <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco Nez de Balboa">
       Vasco Nez de Balboa
      </a>
      heard unexpected news of an "other sea" rich in gold, which he received with great interest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With few resources and using information given by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">
        caciques
       </a>
      </i>
      , he journeyed across the
      <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">
       Isthmus of Panama
      </a>
      with 190 Spaniards, a few native guides, and a pack of dogs.
     </p>
     <p>
      Using a small
      <a href="/wiki/Brigantine" title="Brigantine">
       brigantine
      </a>
      and ten native
      <a href="/wiki/Canoe" title="Canoe">
       canoes
      </a>
      , they sailed along the coast and made landfalls. On September 6, the expedition was reinforced with 1,000 men, fought several battles, entered a dense jungle and climbed the mountain range along the
      <a href="/wiki/Chucunaque_River" title="Chucunaque River">
       Chucunaque River
      </a>
      from where this "other sea" could be seen. Balboa went ahead and, before noon September 25, he saw in the horizon an undiscovered sea, becoming the first European to have seen or reached the Pacific from the New World. The expedition descended towards the shore for a short reconnaissance trip, thus becoming the first Europeans to navigate the Pacific Ocean off the coast of New World. After traveling more than 110km (68mi), Balboa named the bay where they ended up
      <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_San_Miguel" title="Bay of San Miguel">
       <i>
        San Miguel
       </i>
      </a>
      . He named the new sea
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
       <i>
        Mar del Sur
       </i>
       (South Sea)
      </a>
      , since they had traveled south to reach it. Balboa's main purpose in the expedition was the search for gold-rich kingdoms. To this end, he crossed through the lands of
      <i>
       caciques
      </i>
      to the islands, naming the largest one
      <i>
       Isla Rica
      </i>
      (Rich Island, today known as
      <a href="/wiki/Isla_del_Rey_(Panama)" title="Isla del Rey (Panama)">
       Isla del Rey
      </a>
      ). He named the entire group
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Islands" title="Pearl Islands">
        Archipilago de las Perlas
       </a>
      </i>
      , which they still keep today.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Subsequent_developments_to_the_east">
       Subsequent developments to the east
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Subsequent developments to the east">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 15151516, the Spanish fleet led by
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_D%C3%ADaz_de_Sol%C3%ADs" title="Juan Daz de Sols">
       Juan Daz de Sols
      </a>
      , sailed down the east coast of South America as far as
      <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Ro de la Plata">
       Ro de la Plata
      </a>
      , which Sols named shortly before he died, while trying to find a passage to the "South Sea".
     </p>
     <p>
      At the same time, the Portuguese in Southeast Asia made the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Europeans_in_the_Philippines" title="First Europeans in the Philippines">
       first European report on the western Pacific
      </a>
      , having identified
      <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">
       Luzon
      </a>
      east of
      <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">
       Borneo
      </a>
      and named its inhabitants the "
      <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%A7%C3%B5es" title="Lues">
       Lues
      </a>
      ", in the modern
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="First_circumnavigation">
       First circumnavigation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: First circumnavigation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1378" data-file-width="2488" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg/200px-Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg/300px-Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg/400px-Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Magellan%27s_voyage_EN.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Route of
        <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
         Magellan
        </a>
        -
        <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastin Elcano">
         Elcano
        </a>
        world circumnavigation (15191522)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      By 1516 several Portuguese navigators, conflicting with King Manuel I of Portugal, had gathered in
      <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
       Seville
      </a>
      to serve the newly crowned
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
       Charles I of Spain
      </a>
      . Among them were explorers Diogo and
      <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Barbosa" title="Duarte Barbosa">
       Duarte Barbosa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%AAv%C3%A3o_Gomes" title="Estvo Gomes">
       Estvo Gomes
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Joo Serro">
       Joo Serro
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
       Ferdinand Magellan
      </a>
      , cartographers
      <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Reinel" title="Jorge Reinel">
       Jorge Reinel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Ribeiro" title="Diogo Ribeiro">
       Diogo Ribeiro
      </a>
      , cosmographers Francisco and
      <a href="/wiki/Rui_Faleiro" title="Rui Faleiro">
       Ruy Faleiro
      </a>
      and the Flemish merchant
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_de_Haro" title="Christopher de Haro">
       Christopher de Haro
      </a>
      . Ferdinand Magellanwho had sailed in India for Portugal up to 1513, when the
      <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">
       Maluku Islands
      </a>
      were reached, kept contact with
      <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco Serro">
       Francisco Serro
      </a>
      living there
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      developed the theory that the islands were in the
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">
       Tordesillas
      </a>
      Spanish area, supported on studies by Faleiro brothers.
     </p>
     <p>
      Aware of the efforts of the Spanish to find a route to India by sailing west, Magellan presented his plan to Charles I of Spain. The king and Christopher de Haro financed then Magellan's expedition. A fleet was put together, Spanish navigators such as
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastin Elcano">
       Juan Sebastin Elcano
      </a>
      joined the enterprise. On August 10, 1519, departed from Seville a fleet of five ships
      <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">
       flagship
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_(ship)" title="Trinidad (ship)">
        Trinidad
       </a>
      </i>
      under Magellan's command,
      <i>
       San Antonio
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Concepcion
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Santiago
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(ship)" title="Victoria (ship)">
        Victoria
       </a>
      </i>
      , the first being a
      <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">
       caravel
      </a>
      , and all others rated as
      <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">
       carracks
      </a>
      or "naus"with a crew of about 237 men from several nations, with the goal of reaching the Maluku Islands by traveling west, trying to reclaim it under Spain's economic and political sphere.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="759" data-file-width="788" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png/150px-Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png/225px-Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png/300px-Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Detail_from_a_map_of_Ortelius_-_Magellan%27s_ship_Victoria.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(ship)" title="Victoria (ship)">
          Victoria
         </a>
        </i>
        , the single ship to have completed the first world
        <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">
         circumnavigation
        </a>
        . (Detail from
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Maris_Pacifici" title="Maris Pacifici">
          Maris Pacifici
         </a>
        </i>
        by
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ortelius" title="Ortelius">
         Ortelius
        </a>
        , 1589.)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The fleet sailed further and further south, avoiding the Portuguese territories in Brazil, and become the first to reach
      <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">
       Tierra del Fuego
      </a>
      at the tip of the Americas. On October 21, starting in
      <a href="/wiki/Cape_Virgenes" title="Cape Virgenes">
       Cape Virgenes
      </a>
      , began an arduous trip through a 373-mile (600km) long strait that Magellan named
      <i>
       Estrecho de Todos los Santos
      </i>
      , modern
      <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">
       Strait of Magellan
      </a>
      . On November 28, three ships entered the Pacific Oceanthen named
      <i>
       Mar Pacfico
      </i>
      because of its apparent stillness.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The expedition managed to cross the Pacific. Magellan died in the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mactan" title="Battle of Mactan">
       battle of Mactan
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      , leaving the Spaniard
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastin Elcano">
       Juan Sebastin Elcano
      </a>
      the task of completing the voyage, reaching the
      <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">
       Spice Islands
      </a>
      in 1521. On September 6, 1522
      <i>
       Victoria
      </i>
      returned to Spain, thus completing the first
      <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">
       circumnavigation
      </a>
      of the globe. Of the men who set out on five ships, only 18 completed the circumnavigation and managed to return to Spain in this single vessel led by Elcano. Seventeen other arrived later in Spain: twelve captured by the Portuguese in Cape Verde some weeks earlier and between 1525 and 1527, and five survivors of the
      <i>
       Trinidad
      </i>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Pigafetta" title="Antonio Pigafetta">
       Antonio Pigafetta
      </a>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">
       Venetian
      </a>
      scholar and traveler who had asked to be on board and become a strict assistant of Magellan, kept an accurate journal that become the main source for much of what we know about this voyage.
     </p>
     <p>
      This round-the-world voyage gave Spain valuable knowledge of the world and its oceans which later helped in the exploration and settlement of the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      . Although this was not a realistic alternative to the Portuguese route around Africa
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (the
      <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">
       Strait of Magellan
      </a>
      was too far south, and the Pacific Ocean too vast to cover in a single trip from Spain) successive Spanish expeditions used this information to explore the Pacific Ocean and discovered routes that
      <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">
       opened up trade
      </a>
      between
      <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">
       Acapulco
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
       New Spain
      </a>
      (present-day
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
       Mexico
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
       Manila
      </a>
      in the Philippines.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Westward_and_eastward_exploration_meet">
       Westward and eastward exploration meet
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Westward and eastward exploration meet">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tidore.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="640" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tidore.jpg/220px-Tidore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tidore.jpg/330px-Tidore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tidore.jpg/440px-Tidore.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tidore.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        View from
        <a href="/wiki/Ternate" title="Ternate">
         Ternate
        </a>
        to
        <a href="/wiki/Tidore" title="Tidore">
         Tidore
        </a>
        islands in the
        <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">
         Maluku
        </a>
        , where Portuguese Eastward and Spanish Westward explorations ultimately met and clashed between 1522 and 1529
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_85-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-85">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          85
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
         <a href="#cite_note-86">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          86
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saavedras_journey.PNG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="150" data-file-width="300" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Saavedras_journey.PNG/220px-Saavedras_journey.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/Saavedras_journey.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/Saavedras_journey.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saavedras_journey.PNG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Saavedra's failed attempts to find a return route from the Maluku to New Spain (Mexico) in 1527
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Soon after Magellan's expedition, the Portuguese rushed to seize the surviving crew and built a fort in
      <a href="/wiki/Ternate" title="Ternate">
       Ternate
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_85-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1525,
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
       Charles I of Spain
      </a>
      sent another expedition westward to colonize the
      <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">
       Maluku Islands
      </a>
      , claiming that they were in his zone of the
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">
       Treaty of Tordesillas
      </a>
      . The fleet of seven ships and 450 men was led by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garc%C3%ADa_Jofre_de_Loa%C3%ADsa" title="Garca Jofre de Loasa">
       Garca Jofre de Loasa
      </a>
      and included the most notable Spanish navigators:
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastin Elcano">
       Juan Sebastin Elcano
      </a>
      and Loasa, who lost their lives then, and the young
      <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_de_Urdaneta" title="Andrs de Urdaneta">
       Andrs de Urdaneta
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Near the
      <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">
       Strait of Magellan
      </a>
      one of the ships was pushed south by a storm, reaching 56 S, where they thought seeing "
      <i>
       earth's end
      </i>
      ": so
      <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">
       Cape Horn
      </a>
      was crossed for the first time. The expedition reached the islands with great difficulty, docking at
      <a href="/wiki/Tidore" title="Tidore">
       Tidore
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_85-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The conflict with the Portuguese established in nearby Ternate was inevitable, starting nearly a decade of skirmishes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As there was not a set eastern limit to Tordesillas line, both kingdoms organized meetings to resolve the issue. From 1524 to 1529 Portuguese and Spanish experts met at Badajoz-Elvas trying to find the exact location of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antimeridian" title="Antimeridian">
       antimeridian
      </a>
      of Tordesillas, which would divide the world into two equal hemispheres. Each crown appointed three
      <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">
       astronomers
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">
       cartographers
      </a>
      , three
      <a href="/wiki/Navigation" title="Navigation">
       pilots
      </a>
      and three mathematicians.
      <a href="/wiki/Lopo_Homem" title="Lopo Homem">
       Lopo Homem
      </a>
      , Portuguese cartographer and cosmographer was in the board, along with cartographer
      <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Ribeiro" title="Diogo Ribeiro">
       Diogo Ribeiro
      </a>
      on the Spanish delegation. The board met several times, without reaching an agreement: the knowledge at that time was insufficient for an
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_longitude" title="History of longitude">
       accurate calculation of longitude
      </a>
      , and each group gave the islands to its sovereign. The issue was settled only in 1529, after a long negotiation, with the signing of
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zaragoza" title="Treaty of Zaragoza">
       Treaty of Zaragoza
      </a>
      , that attributed the Maluku Islands to Portugal and the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      to Spain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1525 and 1528 Portugal sent several expeditions around the Maluku Islands.
      <a href="/wiki/Gomes_de_Sequeira" title="Gomes de Sequeira">
       Gomes de Sequeira
      </a>
      and Diogo da Rocha were sent north by the governor of Ternate
      <a href="/wiki/Jorge_de_Menezes" title="Jorge de Menezes">
       Jorge de Menezes
      </a>
      , being the first Europeans to reach the
      <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">
       Caroline Islands
      </a>
      , which they named "Islands de Sequeira".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1526, Jorge de Meneses docked on
      <a href="/wiki/Biak" title="Biak">
       Biak
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Waigeo" title="Waigeo">
       Waigeo
      </a>
      islands, Papua New Guinea. Based on these explorations stands the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theory_of_Portuguese_discovery_of_Australia" title="Theory of Portuguese discovery of Australia">
       theory of Portuguese discovery of Australia
      </a>
      , one among several competing theories about the early discovery of Australia, supported by Australian historian
      <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_McIntyre" title="Kenneth McIntyre">
       Kenneth McIntyre
      </a>
      , stating it was discovered by
      <a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3v%C3%A3o_de_Mendon%C3%A7a" title="Cristvo de Mendona">
       Cristvo de Mendona
      </a>
      and Gomes de Sequeira.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1527
      <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernn Corts">
       Hernn Corts
      </a>
      fitted out a fleet to find new lands in the "South Sea" (Pacific Ocean), asking his cousin
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Saavedra_Cer%C3%B3n" title="lvaro de Saavedra Cern">
       lvaro de Saavedra Cern
      </a>
      to take charge. On October 31 of 1527 Saavedra sailed from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">
       New Spain
      </a>
      , crossing the Pacific and touring the north of
      <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">
       New Guinea
      </a>
      , then named
      <i>
       Isla de Oro
      </i>
      . In October 1528 one of the vessels reached Maluku Islands. In his attempt to return to New Spain he was diverted by the northeast
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_wind" title="Trade wind">
       trade winds
      </a>
      , which threw him back, so he tried sailing back down, to south. He returned to New Guinea and sailed northeast, where he sighted the
      <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">
       Marshall Islands
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Islands" title="Admiralty Islands">
       Admiralty Islands
      </a>
      , but again was surprised by the winds, which brought him a third time to the Moluccas. This westbound return route was hard to find, but was eventually discovered by
      <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_de_Urdaneta" title="Andrs de Urdaneta">
       Andrs de Urdaneta
      </a>
      in 1565.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Inland_Spanish_conquistadores_.281519.E2.80.931532.29">
       Inland Spanish
       <i>
        conquistadores
       </i>
       (15191532)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Inland Spanish conquistadores (15191532)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Rumors of undiscovered islands northwest of
      <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">
       Hispaniola
      </a>
      had reached Spain by 1511 and king
      <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">
       Ferdinand II of Aragon
      </a>
      was interested in forestalling further exploration. While Portuguese were making huge gains in the Indian Ocean, the Spanish invested in exploring inland in search of gold and valuable resources. The members of these expeditions, the "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadors" title="Conquistadors">
       conquistadors
      </a>
      ", came from a variety of backgrounds including artisans, merchants, clergy, lesser nobility and freed slaves. They usually supplied their own equipment in exchange for a share in profits, having no direct connection with the royal army, and often no professional military training or experience.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the Americas the Spanish found a number of empires that were as large and populous as those in Europe. However, small bodies of
      <i>
       conquistadors
      </i>
      , with large armies of
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
       Indigenous Americans
      </a>
      groups, managed to conquer these states. During this time,
      <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">
       pandemics
      </a>
      of European disease such as
      <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">
       smallpox
      </a>
      devastated the indigenous populations. Once Spanish
      <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
       sovereignty
      </a>
      was established, the Spanish focused on the extraction and export of gold and silver.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1512, to reward
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Len">
       Juan Ponce de Len
      </a>
      for exploring
      <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
       Puerto Rico
      </a>
      in 1508, king Ferdinand urged him to seek these new lands. He would become governor of discovered lands, but was to finance himself all exploration.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With three ships and about 200 men, Lon set out from Puerto Rico on March 1513. In April they sighted land and named it
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
        La Florida
       </a>
      </i>
      because it was
      <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">
       Easter
      </a>
      (Florida) seasonbelieving it was an island, becoming credited as the first European to land in the continent. The arrival location has been disputed between
      <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">
       St. Augustine
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n_Inlet" title="Ponce de Len Inlet">
       Ponce de Len Inlet
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Beach,_Florida" title="Melbourne Beach, Florida">
       Melbourne Beach
      </a>
      . They headed south for further exploration and on April 8 encountered a current so strong that it pushed them backwards: this was the first encounter with the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">
       Gulf Stream
      </a>
      that would soon become the primary route for eastbound ships leaving the Spanish Indies bound for Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They explored down the coast reaching
      <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">
       Biscayne Bay
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dry_Tortugas" title="Dry Tortugas">
       Dry Tortugas
      </a>
      and then sailing southwest in an attempt to circle
      <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
       Cuba
      </a>
      to return, reaching
      <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">
       Grand Bahama
      </a>
      on July.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cort.C3.A9s.27_Mexico_and_the_Aztec_Empire">
       Corts' Mexico and the Aztec Empire
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Age_of_Discovery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Corts' Mexico and the Aztec Empire">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Spanish conquest of Yucatn">
       Spanish conquest of Yucatn
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Guatemala" title="Spanish conquest of Guatemala">
       Spanish conquest of Guatemala
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="401" data-file-width="931" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg/220px-Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg/330px-Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg/440px-Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ruta_de_Cort%C3%A9s.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Route of Corts inland progress 15191521
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1517
      <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
       Cuba
      </a>
      's governor
      <a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez_de_Cu%C3%A9llar" title="Diego Velzquez de Cullar">
       Diego Velzquez de Cullar
      </a>
      commissioned a fleet under the command of
      <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Hern%C3%A1ndez_de_C%C3%B3rdoba_(Yucat%C3%A1n_conquistador)" title="Francisco Hernndez de Crdoba (Yucatn conquistador)">
       Hernndez de Crdoba
      </a>
      to explore the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_peninsula" title="Yucatn peninsula">
       Yucatn peninsula
      </a>
      . They reached the coast where
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayans" title="Mayans">
       Mayans
      </a>
      invited them to land, but were attacked at night and only a remnant of the crew returned. Velzquez then commissioned another expedition led by his nephew
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Grijalva" title="Juan de Grijalva">
       Juan de Grijalva
      </a>
      , who sailed south along the coast to
      <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">
       Tabasco
      </a>
      , part of the Aztec empire. In 1518 Velzquez gave the mayor of the capital of Cuba,
      <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernn Corts">
       Hernn Corts
      </a>
      , the command of an expedition to secure the interior of Mexico but, due to an old gripe between them, revoked the charter.
     </p>
     <p>
      In February 1519 Corts went ahead anyway, in an act of open mutiny. With about 11 ships, 500 men, 13 horses and a small number of cannons he landed in Yucatn, in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayan_civilization" title="Mayan civilization">
       Mayan
      </a>
      territory,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grunberg_2007_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grunberg_2007-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      claiming the land for the Spanish crown. From
      <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">
       Trinidad
      </a>
      he proceeded to
      <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">
       Tabasco
      </a>
      and won a battle against the natives. Among the vanquished was
      <a href="/wiki/La_Malinche" title="La Malinche">
       La Malinche
      </a>
      , his future mistress, who knew both (Aztec)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">
       Nahuatl language
      </a>
      and Maya, becoming a valuable interpreter and counselor. Through her, Corts learned about the wealthy
      <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">
       Aztec Empire
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In July his men took over
      <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">
       Veracruz
      </a>
      and he placed himself under direct orders of new king
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Spain" title="Charles I of Spain">
       Charles I of Spain
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grunberg_2007_96-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grunberg_2007-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There Corts asked for a meeting with Aztec Emperor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montezuma_II" title="Montezuma II">
       Montezuma II
      </a>
      , who repeatedly refused. They headed to
      <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">
       Tenochtitlan
      </a>
      and on the way made alliances with several tribes. In October, accompanied by about 3,000
      <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcaltec" title="Tlaxcaltec">
       Tlaxcaltec
      </a>
      they marched to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cholula_(Mesoamerican_site)" title="Cholula (Mesoamerican site)">
       Cholula
      </a>
      , the second largest city in central Mexico. Either to instill fear upon the Aztecs waiting for him or (as he later claimed) wishing to make an example when he feared native treachery, they massacred thousands of unarmed members of the nobility gathered at the central plaza and partially burned the city.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1010" data-file-width="1600" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg/220px-Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg/330px-Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg/440px-Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tenochtitlan_y_Golfo_de_Mexico_1524.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of the island city
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenochtitl%C3%A1n" title="Tenochtitln">
         Tenochtitln
        </a>
        and Mexico gulf made by one of Corts' men, 1524,
        <a href="/wiki/Newberry_Library" title="Newberry Library">
         Newberry Library
        </a>
        , Chicago
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
